VII. Public Hearings 
Public Hearing Opened at 6:10 PM by Supervisor Hubbard.  
Greg Bergman from Planning gave overview of site plan and allowable usages 
Many area residents from Long Island spoke about character of Owner of Scott's 
Point, and supported the expansion to include additional usage of a go-cart track 
and pickle ball courts, as well as event and catering space.  
Local Residents Claudette Bianco, Karen Kemp (Zoom), Jennifer Hartenagel Group 
for the Eastend, Barbara Blass and John McAuliff all questioned the usage and 
environmental review as to being unlisted, concerns of fuel spill containment for gas 
operated go-carts, Barbara Blass requested her correspondence prior to meeting be 
incorporated in the hearing notes. 
 
Barbara Blass - Jamesport, NY 
Public Hearing - Island Water Park - January 22, 2025 znz5 JA(-.J l l A 9: O 8 
IWP has the potential to be an exciting recreation destination drawing visitors from 
well beyond town boundaries; success of Island Water Park could be good for 
everyone. Having said that, there ate laws, rules, codes and 
procedures which exist to ensure the health, safety and welfare of people and 
property. IMO, your out-of-court settlement undermines the Town Code setting a 
precedent for future applicants to legally argue they do not need Building Permits, 
Electrical Permits or Certificates of Occupancy either. 
T his site has been developed by an applicant who did what he wanted, when he 
wanted, circumventing that lawful proce?s. You filed a Sum1T1ons and Complaint in NYS 
Supreme Court and rather than allowing an objective Court of Law rule on the Town's 
claims and its merits you settled for $50,000, that's $.50 on the dollar! To put that in 
perspective, the Economic Impact Analysis prepared by NPV anticipates operations to 
generate $65M in annual revenues for Island Water Park. 
I reviewed the LEAF's, the applications and supporting narratives, staff reports, site 
plans, all resolutions of the Town Board, and NYSDEC inspections reports 
as well as the violations and infractions in the Summons and Complaint you 
  
For more information visit our website at www.townofriverheadny.gov  
 
filed with the Court last July. T his historical audit revealed inconsistencies, 
inaccuracies, incomplete submissions and other infractions made by the applicant over 
the years. They are there for all to see. 
This site plan is designed to "legitimize" already constructed, unapproved, 
uninspected, unpermitted development. This implies that the uses, location, 
configuration and intensity would meet the Town's strict standards and 
guidelines for approval in the first place. Think about this, if the parcel were vacant 
and the applicant came in today with this site plan, we'd be looking at a Type 1, 
Pos Dec requiring preparation of an EIS. The Findings Statement would probably 
not support the development that currently exists. 
Instead the SEQRA time clock started with your designating this an Unlisted Action. 
The Town's staff report dated July 29, 2020, for a prior IWP amendment 
says the following, "Based upon the prior SEQRA classification as a Type 1 Action, the 
proposed changes of use and a change to the site plan must be treated (emphasis 
added) as a Type 1 Action pursuant to SEQRA." A Type 1 Action cannot transition to an 
Unlisted Action under SEQRA. 
The latest amendment to legitimize construction of an asphalt go-kart track ½ of a mile 
long, and a catering facility, is also a change to the site plan, and contains a change 
of use and a new use with impacts never previously assessed, (emphasis added) 
yet, it was typed as an Unlisted Action. Based upon the foregoing staff report 
(prepared for the same site and same applicant) why has this recent action not been 
classified as a Type 1? Have you already decided on a Conditional Neg Dec.? 
The integrity of the underlying environmental review process that brought us to this 
point has been compromised. At what stage do the fragmented submissions for 
"amendments" under the Lead Agency's SEQRA review, run afoul of 
Segmentation? Keep in mind that the applicant's EAF said this was not a phased 
development! 
In the Part 1 signed in 2020 for a prior amendment needed to legitimize construction of 
a 75,000 sq ft building, installation of refrigerators, freezers, water heaters, and 
bat.hroom fixtures, wave. pool, etc. states, there will be no additional 
demand for water, no new energy demand, that the site is not over a sole source 
aquifer, and no land use plan or zoning exists for the site, no potential or historical 
contamination at or adjacent to the site, no knowledge of hazardous materials being 
used or buried at or adjacent to the site, yada yada. All inaccurate information. Part 1 
is to be used by the Lead Agency to evaluate potential impacts. The evaluations were 
  
For more information visit our website at www.townofriverheadny.gov  
 
based upon insufficient and inaccurate information. 
The latest Part 1 signed by the applicant in June of 2024 to legitimize construction of a 
go-kart track and pickle ball courts, and change a warehouse to a catering hall should 
also have been rejected for the same reasons. Yet the Town once again, accepted and 
processed the application with a faulty LEAF. Why does the Town continue to take 
the position that when it comes to SEQRA, details don't matter? 
The applicant expects site plan approval in March of 2025 and they do not anticipate 
having to remove the illegal construction and remediate the site since projected 
revenue from the go-karts and catering facility was included in its application 
submitted to the IDA prior to the settlement.. Have the prior site plans been 
completed in accordance with the conditions of approval and verified with 
as-built surveys? Can you produce these records? Who prepared them? If they 
don't exist, exactly what "site plan" is being amended? Can anyone demonstrate 
that mitigation _measures and spec_ial conditions required by prior site plan 
approvals have survived subsequent illegal construction? An internal audit of this 
application is warranted before moving forward. The Unlisted Action was p remature at best. 
VHB submitted a Traffic and Parking Analysis, dated March 2021 which did not include 
the catering facility, the go-kart track, or the pickle ball courts. VHB stated that the 
restaurant would not be open to the public. At that time, the project was described as 
"passive recreation." A lot has changed since then. The most recent application to the 
IDA states, "IWP activities that are in the works include hosting regional and national 
competitions for IWP activities." An updated Traffic and Parking Analysis should be 
provided as part of a Supplemental EIS. 
The site includes an excavated lake pursuant to a mining permit approved by the DEC. 
The mining and reclamation operation is ongoing. According to the on-line DEC 
inspection reports, the mine is not in compliance with the conditions of approval and is 
not consistent with the reclamation plan. The go-kart track, the parking lot and use of 
the lake all violate conditions of the Mined Land Use Plan (MLUP) authorized by the 
DEC and further demonstrates that the applicant has total and consistent disregard for 
rules and regulations at all levels of government. The DEC Region 1 Enforcement 
Coordinator participated in the inspection on 06/12/2024. The inspection report 
included the following: 
"Also on site during th~ inspection: Chris Spies [(NYSDEC Region 1 Enforcement 
Coordinator)]. DEC staff observed a go-kart track had been built at least partially 
in the LOM in the southern half of the property. The approved Mined Land Use 
Plan (MLUP), which includes a reclamation plan and final reclamation objective 
does not include the construction of a go-kart track in the LOM. The go-kart 
  
For more information visit our website at www.townofriverheadny.gov  
 
track constructed in the LOM is a violation of permit condition 1. 
Conformance with Plans. DEC staff also explained to permittee/applicant Eric 
Scott, Cody Scott and other mine site staff that a go-kart track in the LOM does 
not comply with the approved MLUP. DEC staff also observed the site's 
parking lot is significantly larger than the approved plans and is also a 
violation of permit condition 1. Conformance with Plans.") [emphasis 
added]. 
The DEC also warned the applicant that they are prohibited from removing any 
additional material from the site in their efforts to stabilize the slopes; the applicant 
said they intend to lose the material on site. Since there are no as built surveys, how 
can the Town verify that no additional material has been or will be moved off the 
site? Who will supervise the placement of this excavated material since it can 
impact drainage by changing contours and elevations? 
The observations by the DEC are completely inconsistent and override the assertion 
that the DEC is only concerned with stabilizing the slopes of the mine as stated in 
Exhibit 2 of the amended IDA application, to wit: "As Greg Bergman stated in this past 
work session, the DEC is only concerned with the footprint of the lake. Bob Yager of the 
DEC had sent Greg Bergman that information in a previous email several years ago ... " 
It should be noted that Mr. Yager retired several years ago and, according to records, 
has not been on site for general inspections since 10/20/2020; obviously prior to the 
current illegal construction. 
The DEC also observed motorized watercraft in the lake. A site employee said they do 
not intend to use any watercraft with gas/diesel powered motors in the lake. The 
inflatable tube watercraft motors were powered by lithium-ion batteries. Did local 
emergency responders know about that? Information submitted to the agencies 
contains conflicting information about whether the applicant intends to use such 
craft in the future. 
The primary purpose of the initial site plan was the creation of a lake. Based upon its 
approved reclamation plan as a recreational facility it is considered development and 
must be included in lot coverage. What then is the total lot coverage? 
Grading and drainage are Town engineering matters. The rain gardens and drainage 
swales which were part of a previously approved drainage management plan are no 
longer in place. How does that happen? Has the applicant submitted a new 
SWPP? Where is the Town Engineer's report? According to the latest LEAF, an 
additional 2.89 acres of impervious surface will be managed by on-site drainage 
swales ... photos depict drainage pipes with direct outfall into the lake which is 
totally unacceptable. Who approved that? Whether the DEC or the SC DOH 
  
For more information visit our website at www.townofriverheadny.gov  
 
"approve drainage outfall into the lake" as mentioned in the IDA application, is irrelevant 
and beyond the State's and County's jurisdictional involvement. This is a site plan 
matter under the complete control of the Riverhead Town Board. 
Please keep in mind that parts of this facility were constructed and operational without 
receiving electrical permits or inspections, without the required emergency service road, 
and without functioning emergency communications. People were allowed to swim in an 
excavated lake with unstable slopes. We've heard from some of you and are comforted 
by your words that your responsibility to protect life and property weighs more heavily 
on you than anything else. Why then were you not outraged? Your concern appears 
to be situational. 
The aforementioned list of issues and questions is not exhaustive. 
As the Lead Agency, you are answerable to the public on shortcomings of your 
environmental review as well as demonstrating adherence to standard site plan review 
and safety procedures. 
So how do we proceed? Think of it this way ... if a hockey team scores a goal and their 
opponents challenge the play for being offside the play gets reviewed by the booth 
which could overturn or confirm the goal. If the tape confirms that the play was indeed 
offside, the goal is overturned. The game continues and the score returns to what it was 
before the infraction, no goal. No circumstances or conditions financial or otherwise 
would allow the team to keep that goal. After reviewing IWP's record the call should be 
no goal. 
The Town should rescind its Unlisted Action. A comprehensive review to determine 
appropriate mitigation of cumulative impacts particularly as they relate to traffic, parking 
and drainage is warranted. 
Finally, when the applicant was asked for a response to being issued a stop work order 
in 2021 according to Riverheadlocal he said, "So if I've been breaking the rules for 24 
years, nobody's said anything to me for 24 years." It's time to say something, no goal! 
This site plan amendment should not be approved. 
Thank you, Barbara Blass, Jamesport 
  - 6:00 PM Public Hearing Island Water Park Site Plan

NOTICE OF MEETING FOR RIVERHEAD TOWN BOARD & RIVERHEAD TOWN 
COMMUNITY DEVELOPMENT AGENCY  
 
PLEASE TAKE NOTICE that the Town Board Meeting and Riverhead Community 
Development Agency, New York (the “CDA”) meeting scheduled for January 22, 2025 at 
6:00 p.m. at Riverhead Town Hall, 4 W Second St, Riverhead, New York shall proceed as 
scheduled.     
PLEASE TAKE FURTHER NOTICE, that in addition to in person attendance, the 
public can watch the January 22, 2025  meetings of the Town Board & CDA via the 
following methods:  
1. Live stream; namely, by viewing it on your television on Channel 22;  
2. Logging on the Town of Riverhead website, www. townofriverheadny.gov and 
clicking on the link “Channel 22” on Quick Links on the home page or by connecting to 
the URL, which is as follows: townofriverheadny.viebit.com/player_live.php  
3. Zoom Meeting, log in as follows: 
    https://us02web.zoom.us/j/86910279688?pwd=Lbf9T47CdWHkTz4Mv71FraSGKC2vKU.1 
 
Webinar ID:  869 1027 9688   Passcode:  809091 
Dial by your location: +1 929 205 6099 (New York)

person will have an opportunity to  be heard, via Zoom, to make their comments and/or 
raise questions regarding any scheduled  public hearings and resolutions  under 
consideration, as applicable, before the CDA & the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead 
at their respective January 22, 2025 meetings, and further participate in the open 
comment period on any matter at the conclusion of the Agenda.

via Zoom are as follows:

request to speak.

unmuted and visible for the five -minute comment period. After five minutes, you will be 
placed back in the audience.

NOTICE OF PUBLIC HEARING 
 
PLEASE TAKE NOTICE that a public hearing will be held before the Town Board of the 
Town of Riverhead at 4 West 2nd Street, Riverhead, New York, on the 22nd day of January, 
2025, at or about 6:00 p.m., to consider a site plan application submitted by Island Water 
Park seeking to legalize a go -kart track, pickleball courts, and conversion of an interior 
storage space to a catering/event space on a 41.9 acre pa rcel of land located at 5835 
Middle Country Road, Calverton, NY, located within the Planned Recreational Park (PRP) 
zoning use district, and more particularly described as SCTM No. 600-135-1-7.34.

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-89 
 
BUDGET ADOPTION OF COMMUNITY BENEFIT FUNDS FOR OPEN SPACE 
PROJECT 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution # 397-2019 adopted on May 22, 2019, the Town 
Board did authorize and approve a Community Benefits Agreement between Riverhead 
Solar I and the Town; and 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to the terms of the Community Benefits Agreement, the 
Town will administer the funds for the purposes set forth in the Community Benefits 
Agreement; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Open Space Committee requested that the Town Board approve 
expenditure of Community Benefit Funds for enhancement of public access to lands 
preserved for public access and appeared/presented updates on open space 
preservation efforts and desired improvements, cost estimates provided by the 
Engineering Department, to several open space preservation parcels; and 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution # 634-2021, adopted on October 5, 2021, the Town 
Board approved the budget adoption and establishment of capital project #72119 for the 
improvement of the Sound Avenue Preserve, funded by the Community Benefit Funds 
in the amount of $12,000; and 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution # 180-2024, the Recreation Superintendent 
determined that the capital project for the Sound Avenue Preserve improvements has 
been completed for a cost of $2,478.37 and returned the unspent funds of $9,521.63 
back to the Restricted Fund Balance for the Community Benefit Funds, as part of the LI 
Solar/S Power agreement held in the General Fund; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Open Space Committee has requested that the Town Board 
approve expenditures using a portion of the remaining Community Benefit Funds, in the 
amount of $500, for the purchase of materials to construct a kiosk structure at the 
Sound Avenue Preserve. This kiosk will be voluntarily built by the Boy Scouts of 
America Foundation and will provide information about the natural features and trail 
information at the property; and 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to the funding category Promotion and Protection of 
Agriculture and Open Space Initiative, funds may be expended to achieve or be in 
9.1
Packet Pg. 117
furtherance of preservation of farmland, open space...establishment of nature 
preserves, preservation of public access to lands for public use. 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Supervisor be, and is hereby 
authorized to establish the following budget adjustments; 
 
  
 
 FROM  TO 
 
A01-899-100-00000 Restricted Fund Balance  $500.00 
  
A01-7-7110-415-000-00000 Parks – Supplies      $500.00 
 
And be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a copy of this 
resolution to finance@townofriverheadny.gov, Recreation and Purchasing Departments, 
and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-90 
 
FUND BALANCE BUDGET TRANSFER FOR CODE ENFORCEMENT VEHICLE 
PURCHASE 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, Town Board Resolution 2024-682 approved a budget transfer into 
the budget line ‘Code Enforcement Vehicles’ in the amount of $33,000 for the 
replacement of a Code Enforcement vehicle that has reached the end of its useful life 
and is no longer cost-effective to maintain, and 
 
WHEREAS, the funds transferred were not expended in 2024 due to a lack of 
inventory and the inability to locate an appropriate vehicle. And as such, the funds 
reverted back to fund balance at the close of the 2024 budget year, and 
 
WHEREAS, it’s necessary to reinstate this budget from the fund balance in order 
to proceed with the purchase of the replacement Code Enforcement vehicle,  
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Supervisor is hereby authorized 
to make the following budget adjustments; 
  
 FROM  TO 
 
A01-9999-000-00000-0 – Fund Balance                  $33,000 
           
             A01-3-3625-280-000-00000  
Code Enforcement Vehicles                                   $33,000 
 
 
AND BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to 
forward a copy of this resolution to finance@townofriverheadny.gov, Town Attorney, 
Purchasing, and Code Enforcement departments. And be it further 
 
RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
SECONDER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

AUTHORIZES SEWER DISTRICT EMPLOYEES TO ATTEND NYWEA MEETING 
AND TRAINING CONFERENCE 
 
Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
WHEREAS, The New York Water Environment Association (NYWEA) is holding 
it’s annual meeting and training conference February 3 through February 5, 2025 in 
New York City; and 
 
 
WHEREAS, it is the desire of Michael Reichel, Sewer District Superintendent 
and Assistant Sewer Superintendent, Tim Allen to attend this conference: and 
 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board of the Town of 
Riverhead hereby authorizes Sewer District Superintendent Michael Reichel and 
Assistant Sewer Superintendent, Tim Allen to attend the aforementioned conference to 
be held at Marriott Convention Center in New York City on February 3 through February 
5, 2025; and be it further 
 
 
RESOLVED, that all related, receipted, expenses incurred by the aforementioned 
employees shall not exceed a total cost of $1,165.00 each and shall be reimbursed 
upon their return in accordance with the Town of Riverhead Travel Policy; and be it 
further 
 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward copies of this 
resolution to reichel@townofriverheadny.gov, the Accounting Department and the Office 
of the Town Attorney; and be it further 
 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a cop of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-93 
 
AUTHORIZES THE ATTENDANCE BY DEPUTY TOWN ATTORNEY CERU AT THE 
2025 ANNUAL MEETING & TRAINING SCHOOL HELD BY THE ASSOCIATION OF 
TOWNS 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, the Association of Towns is hosting their 2025 Training School and 
Annual Meeting at the New York Marriott Marquis (Times Square), located at 1535 
Broadway, New York City, New York, on Sunday, February 16, 2025 t hrough 
Wednesday, February 19, 2025; and  
 
WHEREAS, it is the desire of Victoria Ceru, Deputy Town Attorney to attend 
such course; and 
 
 WHEREAS, the cost of the conference for Deputy Town Attorney Ceru, with 
Attorney Continuing Legal Education (10 Profess ional Practice/Skills credits and 2 
Ethics credits) is $465.00, with related expenses incidental to attending said 
conference. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board of the Town of 
Riverhead hereby authorizes Deputy Town Attorney Ceru to atte nd the Association of 
Towns 2025 Training School and Annual Meeting to be held at the New York Marriott 
Marquis (Times Square), New York City, New York on Sunday, February 16, 2025  
through Wednesday, February 19, 2025; and be it further,  
 
            RESOLVED, that all related, receipted, expenses incurred shall be reimbursed 
upon her return in accordance with the Town of Riverhead Travel Policy; and be it 
further, 
  
 RESOLVED, that the Town Board hereby authorizes payment of the meeting fee 
for Deputy Town Attorney Ceru, including CLE fees, totaling $465.00; and be it further 
RESOLVED, that the Town Board hereby authorizes overnight accommodations 
to be limited to two evenings, Sunday, February 16, 2025 and Monday, February 17, 
2025 at the New York Marriott Marquis (Times Square); and be it further,   
 
RESOLVED, that approved related expenses incurred by Deputy Town Attorney 
Ceru will be reimbursed upon proper submission of receipts and in accordance with the 
Town of Riverhead Travel and Conference Policy; and be it further,   
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward copies of this 
resolution to the Accounting Department and Deputy Town Attorney Ceru; and be it 
further, 
9.5
Packet Pg. 160
 
 RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a co py of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a copy of same may be 
obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

TB Resolution 2025-94 
 
AUTHORIZES TOWN JUSTICE TO ATTEND TRAINING CONFERENCE 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, the NYS Office of Justice Court Support is conducting its 2025 Town 
& Village Justices Continuing Education Program from Wednesday March 19, 2025 to 
Thursday March 20, 2024 in Niagara Falls, NY; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Justice Court has requested authorization for one Town Justice 
to attend said Program 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Justice Court is authorized to 
send Judge Sean M. Walter to attend the 2025 Town & Village Justices Continuing 
Education Program in Niagara Falls, NY; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that all related expenses incurred shall not exceed a total cost of 
$940.00 (expenses to include fees for registration, meals, lodging and other travel costs 
such as mileage, tolls and gas) shall be reimbursed upon their return and in accordance 
with the Town’s Travel and Conference Policy; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
SECONDER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-95 
 
APPOINTS AN ACCOUNT CLERK 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, Melanie DiNizio has been serving as a provisional appointment in 
the position of Account Clerk since September 23, 2204; and 
 
WHEREAS, on January 10, 2025 the Suffolk County Department of Civil Service 
established a certified List of Eligibles, list # 25AF030, for the position of Account Clerk, 
and Melanie DiNizio is immediately reachable on the County List; and 
 
WHEREAS, Civil Service regulations require that a permanent appointment of a 
provisional employee be made within sixty days of the date a Certified List of Eligibles is 
first established.  
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that pursuant to Civil Service 
regulations, this Town Board hereby removes the provisional status of Melanie DiNizio 
and appoints her to the title of Account Clerk effective today, January 22, 2025 at no 
change to her current salary or other level of benefits. 
 
RESOLVED, that Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device, and if needed, a certified copy of same 
can be obtained from the office of the Town Clerk.  
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

APPOINTS A SITE PLAN REVIEWER 
 
Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
WHEREAS, there is a need for a Site Plan Reviewer in the Planning  division of 
the Economic Development and Planning Department; and 
 
WHEREAS, Suffolk County Department of Civil Service established a certified 
List of Eligibles, list # 25AF043, for the position of Site Plan Reviewer, and current Town 
employee Marisa Danowski is immediately reachable and her Department Head is 
willing to appoint her to same; and  
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, the Town Board hereby appoints Marisa 
Danowski to the title of Site Plan Reviewer effective March 10, 2025 at a salary group 7 
step P found on the CSEA Administrative salary schedule of $75,720.45 prorated in the 
year 2025. 
 
RESOLVED, a copy of this resolution will be forwarded to Dawn Thomas 
Community Development Supervisor, Marisa Danowski and Payroll.  All Town Hall 
Departments may review and obtain a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage 
device and if needed, a certified copy of same may be obtained from the Office of the 
Town Clerk.

01.22.2025 TABLED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-97 
 
APPOINTS ALEXANDER ESCOBAR TO THE ANTI-BIAS TASK FORCE 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
 WHEREAS, by Resolution 32023-688 adopted on September 6, 2023, the Town 
Board did appoint Officers and Members to the Anti-Bias Task Force; and  
  
 WHEREAS, such Resolution #2023-688 empowers the Town Board to appoint 
additional members to the Anti-Bias Task Force; and 
 
WHEREAS, a vacancy presently exists on the Anti-Bias Task Force due to the 
unfortunate passing of Reverend Janet Wright, whom the Task Force and all involved 
would like to express sincere appreciation for all of her efforts and dedication; and 
 
WHEREAS, Alexander Escobar has expressed interest in serving on the Anti-
Bias Task Force; and 
 
 NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board of the Town of 
Riverhead hereby appoints Alexander Escobar to the Riverhead Anti-Bias Task Force to 
assume the (2) year term of Rev. Janice Wright without compensation, which term shall 
expire on September 30, 2025 and who shall serve at the pleasure of the Town Board 
and on a voluntary basis without salary; and be it further      
  
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward a copy of this 
resolution to the Town Board Coordinator and the Town of Riverhead Anti-Bias Task 
Force; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.  
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: TABLED [UNANIMOUS]
 
Next: 2/19/2025 6:00 PM 
MOVER: Tim Hubbard, Supervisor 
SECONDER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

APPOINTS A PART-TIME TRAFFIC CONTROL SPECIALIST 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, Part-time Traffic Control Specialists are needed at the Riverhead 
Police Department to direct pedestrians and vehicular traffic during special events, 
issue summonses, and enforce rules and regulations relating to the parking, standing 
and stopping of vehicles; and  
 
WHEREAS, an interview was conducted and a recommendation of a suitable 
candidate has been made by the supervising police officer.  
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that effective January 23, 2025, and 
pursuant to a successfully completed background investigation, and drug and alcohol 
testing administered by the Town, this Town Board hereby appoints Ryan Ott to the 
position of Part-time Traffic Control Specialist at an hourly rate of $21.00. 
 
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward 
a copy of this resolution to Ryan Ott, the Chief of Police, the Personnel Officer and the 
Financial Administrator. Town Hall departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device. 
 
THE VOTE

MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-107 
 
AUTHORIZES THE FILING OF AN APPLICATION FOR  NEW YORK STATE 
ASSISTANCE FROM THE HOUSEHOLD HAZARDOUS WASTE (HHW) STATE 
ASSISTANCE PROGRAM AND SIGNING OF THE ASSOCIATED STATE 
CONTRACT, UNDER THE APPROPRIATE LAWS OF NEW YORK STATE 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, the State of New York provides financial aid for hazardous waste 
programs for 50% of the eligible expenses for calendar year 2024; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead herein called the MUNICIPALITY, has 
examined and duly considered the applicable laws of the State of New York and the 
MUNICIPALITY deems it to be in the public interest and benefit to file an application 
under these laws; and 
 
WHEREAS, it is necessary that a Contract by and between THE PEOPLE OF 
THE STATE OF NEW YORK, herein called the STATE, and the MUNICIPALITY be 
executed for such STATE Aid for 2024 HHW Program funding to reimburse expenses 
already incurred for FY2023; 
 
 THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Riverhead Town Board: 
 
1. That the filing of an application in the form required by the State of New York in 
conformity with the applicable laws of the State of New York including all 
understanding and assurances contained in said application is hereby authorized; 
 
2. That the Supervisor, or his designee is directed and authorized as the official 
representative of the MUNICIPALITY to act in connection with the application and to 
provide such additional information as may be required and to sign the resulting 
contract if said application is approved by the STATE; 
 
3. That the MUNICIPALITY agrees that it will fund the entire cost of said household 
hazardous waste program and will be reimbursed by the STATE for the STATE 
share of such costs; 
 
4. That this resolution shall take effect immediately.  
 
THEREFORE, BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk shall provide 
a copy of this resolution to the Community Development Department and Town 
Engineer Drew Dillingham. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
9.19
Packet Pg. 195
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-108 
 
AUTHORIZES RENEWAL OF A MUSICAL WORKS LICENSE AGREEMENT WITH 
THE AMERICAN SOCIETY OF COMPOSERS, AUTHORS AND PUBLISHERS 
(ASCAP) 2025 
 
Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead plays pre -recorded music in the form of 
digital audio files, compact discs, digital video discs, cassettes, and other media in 
Town facilities and at Town events (e.g. the Senior Center, teen activities); and  
 
WHEREAS, many of these works are protected by U.S. Copyright Law; and  
 
WHEREAS, a municipality requires permission from the holders of such 
copyrights to use the works in a public forum; and  
 
WHEREAS, the American Society of Compo sers, Authors and Publishers 
(ASCAP) represents the holders of copyrights for over eight million such works; and  
 
WHEREAS, ASCAP offers a license granting permission to municipalities for the 
purpose of playing all of the works of copyright holders ASCAP represents; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead wishes to renew a license agreement with 
ASCAP for the right to play pre -recorded music authorized for use by ASCAP for the 
period January 1, 2025 to December 31, 2025 in the amount of $445.00. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board hereby authorizes 
renewal of a license agreement with ASCAP for the right to play pre -recorded music 
authorized for use by ASCAP for the period January 1, 202 5, to December 31, 202 5, in 
the amount of $445.00; and  
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby directed to forward a copy of 
this resolution to the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it further  
 
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED , that all Town Hall Departments may review and 
obtain a copy of this resolution from t he electronic storage device and, if needed, a 
certified copy of same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.  
 
THE VOTE

MOVER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-109 
 
AUTHORIZES THE SUPERVISOR TO EXECUTE AN ADDENDUM TO AN 
AGREEMENT WITH LVF LANDSCAPE ARCHITECTS, PLLC (STREETSCAPE) 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
 WHEREAS, The Town of Riverhead executed a Consultant/ Professional 
Services Agreement with LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC dated March 22, 2024 for 
design and development consulting services relating to Town Square and Streetscape 
Improvements; and 
 
 WHEREAS, LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC wishes to add Land, Air, Water 
Environmental Services, Inc., a Geotech Boring consultant, as an additional member of 
its support team tasked with collecting pavement core samples relating to the Town of 
Riverhead Streetscapes DOT permits; and 
 
WHEREAS, Land, Air, Water Environmental Services, Inc., has a business 
address of 32 Chichester Avenue, Center Moriches, New York 11934; and 
 
WHEREAS, the change proposed by LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC shall not 
materially affect any other term of the executed Consultant/Professional Services 
Agreement or amounts authorized to be paid to LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Supervisor is hereby 
authorized to execute an addendum to the agreement with LVF Landscape Architects, 
PLLC in substantially the same form as annexed hereto; and be it further,     
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward a copy of this 
resolution to Dawn Thomas, CDA Director, Accounting Department and the Office of the 
Town Attorney; and be it further,   
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

Packet Pg. 206
Attachment: Addendum 2-STREETSCAPE  (2025-109 : Authorizes the Supervisor to Execute Addendum with LVF Landscape Architects
 
01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-110 
 
AUTHORIZES THE SUPERVISOR TO EXECUTE AN ADDENDUM TO AN 
AGREEMENT WITH LVF LANDSCAPE ARCHITECTS, PLLC (PLAYGROUND) 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
 WHEREAS, The Town of Riverhead executed a Consultant/ Professional 
Services Agreement with LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC dated January 22, 2024 for 
the Planning, Design and Engineering of the Proposed Town Square Adaptive 
Playground adjacent to the planned new Town Square; and 
 
 WHEREAS, LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC presented engineering 
alternatives for the Town of Riverhead Riverfront Adaptive Playground and Town of 
Riverhead “lower town square” in response to the updated construc tion cost estimate; 
and 
 
WHEREAS, the engineering alternative selected by the Town requires a 
redesign of certain features creating additional consulting services totaling $13,920.00. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED,  that LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC 
shall be entitled to additional compensation totaling $13,290.00 to complete the 
requested design change and all terms and conditions of the original 
Consultant/Professional Services Agreement dated January 22, 2024 shall remain in full 
force and effect; and be it further,     
 
RESOLVED, that the Supervisor is hereby authorized to execute an addendum 
to the agreement with LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC in substantially the same form 
as annexed hereto; and be it further,   
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is here by directed to forward a copy of this 
resolution to Dawn Thomas, CDA Director, Accounting Department and the Office of the 
Town Attorney; and be it further,   
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
SECONDER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

Attachment: Addendum2-PLAY  (2025-110 : Authorize Supervisor to Execute Addendum with LVF Landscape Architects (Playground))
 
01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-111 
 
GRANTS CHAPTER 229 EXCAVATION/EXPORTATION PERMIT FOR GR 
RIVERHEAD LAND LLC (WASHVILLE) 1535 OLD COUNTRY ROAD, RIVERHEAD, 
NY  SCTM NO. 600-101-2-12.6 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, the Planning Board, by Resolution No. 2023-084, dated October 5, 
2023, granted approval for the site plan application of 1535 Old Country Road, to permit 
the construction of a 3,975 sq.ft. one-story self-service car wash that will be fully 
automated with payment kiosks and a limited number of employees, new landscaping, 
and other site improvements, upon real property located at 1535 Old Country Road 
Riverhead, NY, more particularly described as SCTM No. 600-101-2-12.6; and  
 
WHEREAS, GR Riverhead Land, LLC, has submitted a Chapter 229 
Excavation/Exportation permit to allow for the excavation and exportation of 7,040 cubic 
yards of earthen material from this parcel; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Building Department is in receipt of an earthwork plan, signed 
and sealed by Douglas E. Adams, PE, LS, last dated November 20, 2024, in 
accordance with the approved site plan; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board has reviewed and considered the application for the 
aforementioned excavation/exportation permit.  Now, therefore be it 
 
RESOLVED, that based upon the forgoing, the Town Board hereby grants the 
Chapter 229 Excavation/Exportation permit requested by the application, to authorize 
the excavation and exportation of 7,040 cubic yards of material in accordance with the 
approved site plan and earthwork calculations aforementioned; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, the Building Department is hereby authorized to accept and collect 
a permit fee of $14,080.00; representing $2.00 per cubic yard for the exportation of said 
soils, in addition to a permit fee of $100.00; and be it further  
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to send a certified copy of 
this resolution to the Building Department, the Planning Department; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may obtain a copy of this resolution 
from the electronic storage device; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that a certified copy of this resolution may be obtained from the 
Town Clerk’s office by request.   
 
THE VOTE 
9.23
Packet Pg. 210
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-112 
 
AMENDS RESOLUTION #86-2025 SETTING FEES FOR TAXICABS AND VEHICLES 
FOR HIRE PURSUANT TO CHAPTER 281 OF THE RIVERHEAD TOWN CODE 
 
Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
WHEREAS, On January 7, 2025 the Town Board adopted resolution 86-2025, 
and  
 
WHEREAS, The Town Board is amending resolution 86-2025 to reflect corrected 
and additional increased taxcab permit fees,  
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, effective January 22, 
2025, the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead, hereby established the following fee 
schedule pursuant to Chapter 281 of the Riverhead Town Code: 
 
Fee for an owner's license:      $750.00 
Fee for a vehicle permit:      $200.00 per vehicle 
Fee for an operator's permit:     $200.00 
Fee for an appeal of a disapproval,  
suspension hearing or revocation hearing:   $100.00 
 
Late fee:        $50.00 
 
Renewal fees: 
  
Owner's license:     $375.00 
 
Vehicle permit:     $150.00 
 
Operator's permit:      $150.00 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

Packet Pg. 216
Chapter 207. Animals 
 
Article I. Dogs and Domestic/ Farm Animals 
 
 
§ 207-3Application for license. 
A. Applications for a one-year license or a renewal thereof shall be accompanied by a 
nonrefundable processing fee of $9for an altered dog and $15 for an unaltered dog. Applications 
for a three-year license or renewal thereof shall be accompanied by a nonrefundable processing 
fee of $27 for an altered dog and $45 for an unaltered dog established by resolution of the 
Town Board of the Town of Riverhead. In the case of an altered dog, a portion of the fee in the 
amount of $1 and, in the case of an unaltered dog, a portion of the fee in the amount of $3 shall 
be paid over to the agency designated pursuant to Article 7 of the Agriculture and Markets Law 
to be used for animal population control efforts. An application for a license or renewal shall be 
in the form prescribed by the Riverhead Town Clerk and shall provide for the following 
minimum information: 
(1) The name, residence address and telephone number of each owner; 
(2) The name, sex, approximate age, breed, color, markings and other identifying details of the 
dog; 
(3) Whether the dog has been spayed or neutered; and 
(4) Such other information or documentation deemed necessary by the Town Clerk to effectuate 
the purpose of this article. 
B. Rabies certification. The application for a license or renewal shall be accompanied by a 
statement certified by a licensed veterinarian showing that the dog has received the rabies 
vaccine; or, in lieu thereof, a statement certified by a licensed veterinarian that because of the 
dog's age or other reason, the life of the dog would be endangered by the administration of the 
vaccine. 
C. In the case of an altered dog, every application shall be accompanied by a certificate signed 
by a licensed veterinarian or a sworn affidavit signed by the owner in the form acceptable to the 
Town Clerk showing that the dog has been spayed or neutered, except that such certificate or 
affidavit is not required if same is already on file with the Town Clerk. In lieu of the spay or 
neuter certificate, an owner may present a statement certified by a licensed veterinarian stating 
that he or she has examined the dog and found that because of old age or other reason, the life of 
the dog would be endangered by spaying or neutering. In such case, the license fee for the dog 
shall be the same as an altered dog. 
D. No individual under the age of 18 years shall be deemed an owner of record and be issued a 
dog license. 
§ 207-4Issuance of license; transferability; identification tag. 
A. Upon validation by the Town Clerk or authorized Dog Control Officer, a dog license shall be 
issued and a record of its issuance retained in the office of the Town Clerk. Such record shall be 
made available upon request to the State Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets, or successor 
thereof. 
B. No license shall be transferable. Upon the transfer of ownership of any dog, the new owner 
shall immediately apply for a new license for the dog. A license cannot be transferred to another 
dog. 
C. Identification tag. 
9.25.a
Packet Pg. 217
Attachment: 207 Full Text as amended  (2025-113 : Authorizes Town Clerk to Publish Notice of Public Hearing Chapter 207 Dog License)
(1) The Town Clerk shall assign an identification number to a dog when it is first licensed. Such 
identification number shall be carried by the dog on an identification tag which shall be affixed 
to the collar of the dog at all times, except that the tag is not required to be worn while the dog is 
participating in a dog show. In addition, all identification tags shall name the Town of Riverhead, 
200 Howell Avenue, Riverhead, New York State 11901, and name the Town of Riverhead's 
main telephone number. 
(2)  No tag carrying an identification number shall be affixed to the collar of any dog other than 
the one to which the number has been assigned. 
(3) Any person wishing to replace a tag previously issued shall pay the sum of $3 established by 
resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead to the Town Clerk for a replacement 
tag. 
 
 
***UNCHANGED PARAGRAPHS OMITTED* 
 
A.  
Unidentified dogs. Each dog which is not identified, whether or not licensed, shall be held for a 
period of five days from the day seized. 
[Amended 2-20-2013 by L.L. No. 2-2013] 
(1) During the first five days the dog may be redeemed by its owner, provided that such owner 
produces proof that the dog has been licensed and has been identified pursuant to the provisions 
of Article 7 of the New York State Agriculture and Markets Law, as well as the following 
impoundment fees established by resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead. 
(a) Twenty dollars for the first impoundment of any dog owned by that person. 
(b) Forty dollars for the first 24 hours or part thereof and $5 for each additional 24 hours or part 
thereof for the second impoundment within one year of the first impoundment of any dog owned 
by that person. 
(c) Sixty dollars for the first 24 hours or part thereof and $5 for each additional 24 hours or part 
thereof for the third and subsequent impoundments within one year of the first impoundment of 
any dog owned by that person. 
(2) After a period of five days, such unidentified dog shall be available for adoption.

Chapter 257. Peddling and Soliciting 
 
Article I. Licensing and Solicitation 
 
§ 257-7 Fees. 
A. The license fee payable by each peddler for each unit, truck or any conveyance carrying wares 
shall be established by resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead. as follows: 
(1) Per year: $100.  
(2) Per six months: $75.  
(3) Per three months: $50.  
 
 
B. The license fee for each solicitor or canvasser going from house to house shall be established 
by resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead. as follows: 
(1) Per year: $75.  
(2) Per six months: $50.  
(3) Per three months: $25.

01.22.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-116 
 
RESOLUTION CALLING PUBLIC HEARING REGARDING A CAPITAL 
IMPROVEMENT FOR THE EXTENSION (NO. 97) OF BOUNDARIES AND 
FACILITIES OF THE RIVERHEAD WATER DISTRICT FOR FORGE ROAD, 
CALVERTON, NEW YORK AT THE PROPERTIES KNOWN AS SCTM DISTRICT 
0600, SECTION 118, BLOCK 5, LOTS 1.1, 1.2, 2 THROUGH 11 AND 12.1; SECTION 
119, BLOCK 2, LOTS 59 THROUGH 62; AND SECTION 139, BLOCK 1, LOTS 1 
THROUGH 4 
 
Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
WHEREAS, The Town of Riverhead (Town) has identified the need to extend the 
boundaries of the service area of the Riverhead Water District (District) along with its 
existing distribution facilities to serve approximately sev enty mobile home, and fourteen 
single family residences currently receiving potable drinking water from private wells. 
Limited water quality data for the private wells, indicates detections of contaminants or a 
likely potential for contamination in the for m of poly and per -fluoroalkyl substances 
(PFAS), arsenic, iron, and manganese. These wells are located adjacent to or within 
close proximity of the Peconic River and Peconic Lake, however the source of the non -
naturally occurring contaminants is unknown. T he extension of clean water facilities is 
desirous now as wells are beginning to be impacted and the contamination level has 
been detected as approaching New York State drinking water standards. The District 
seeks to provide clean potable water through the  installation of approximately 2,800 
linear feet of water main at a projected revised cost of $1,520,000.00 exclusive of the 
costs related to installation of private service lines and key monies to be borne by 
property owners. 
 
WHEREAS, the boundary of sai d proposed extension is set forth fully in the 
attached Exhibit A, and  
 
WHEREAS, a revised map and plan dated November 2024 has been prepared 
by H2M, consulting engineers to the Riverhead Water District, detailing the necessary 
measures and costs associat ed with extending the Riverhead Water District facilities to 
service the subdivision and the development site and proposed residences; and  
 
WHEREAS, the map and plan are available for review and inspection at the 
Office of the Riverhead Town Clerk, 4 West  Second Street, Riverhead, New York, 
during normal business hours; and   
 
WHEREAS, said map and plan calls for an extension of the existing water 
facilities and boundaries to provide service to approximately seventy mobile homes, and 
fourteen single family  residences. The proposed extension is situated such that the 
District’s low pressure zone facilities can be extended from an existing 12 -inch cement 
lined ductile iron pipe just north of NYS Route 25 on the southern end of Kroemer 
9.28
Packet Pg. 228
Avenue. A total of appro ximately 2,800 linear feet of new 8 -inch water main will be 
required to serve the extension area. Each residential dwelling will receive a 1” water 
service. The mobile home parks will receive either 4” or 2” water service based upon 
their respective sizes. For firefighting purposes, five new fire hydrant assemblies will be 
required to provide the proper fire protection. A proposed layout of the proposed water 
mains and appurtenances and hydrants is contained was an exhibit to the map and 
plan. 
 
WHEREAS, the estimated project cost to implement Extension No. 97 has been 
estimated at $1,520,000.00. These costs also include engineering, permitting, 
construction observation, legal, administration, contingencies, but excluding District Key 
Money Fees and installation of private water mains. (further mentioned below); and 
 
WHEREAS, On March 15, 2023, the Town was informed the project received 
grant funding under the 2022 Bipartisan Infrastructure Law – Emerging Contaminants 
for the full project cost or $1,185,000.00 . The balance of funds required to fund the 
project shall be from the Town Community Preservation Fund; and 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution #814 adopted on September 17, 2024, the Town 
Board amended Chapter 221 to create advisory board known as the Community 
Preservation Fund Water Quality Improvement & Pollution Prevention Committee with 
the duty and responsibility to make recommendations to the Town Board for 
identification of and/or set criteria for water quality improvement activities or pollution 
prevention projects to be included in the Town’s Community Preservation Fund Project 
Plan and by Resolution #877 adopted on October 16, 2024, the Town did adopt an 
amendment to the Community Preservation Fund Project Plan setting forth criteria for 
water quality improvement activities or pollution prevention projects; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Community Preservation Fund Water Quality Improvement & 
Pollution Prevention Committee have reviewed this project, Extension 97, and 
determined that such project meets the criteria and re commends that the Town Board 
authorize expenditure from Community Preservation Fund in the amount of  
$335,000.000 (total cost $1,520,000.00 less grant $1,185,000.00) necessary for fund 
project with each resident will be responsible for the installation of  their private service 
line from the meter pit to the residence including cost of the water meter, backflow 
prevention where appropriate, connection to internal plumbing, disconnect of existing 
private well from in -house plumbing or community water piping and well abandonment; 
and 
 
WHEREAS, the single -family homes currently on private wells that have the 
potential to be or have already been impacted by contamination are exempt from Key 
Money Fees. The existing commercial mobile home parks are subject to Key  Money 
Fees of $2,047 per mobile home unit. For the estimated seventy mobile homes spread 
across three properties the total Key Money Assessment is $143,290; and  
 
WHEREAS, the proposed extension of water mains will be solely located within 
the public righ t-of-way of the Town of Riverhead and involves the extension of public 
water utilities to aid in the upgrade or replacement of private drinking water wells due to 
their impact or high susceptibility to being impacted by contamination. Based on the 
guidelines provided by the New York State Department of Environmental Conservation 
(NYSDEC) in 6 NYCRR Part 617.5, the project can be considered a Type II project, 
requiring no further review; and  
9.28
Packet Pg. 229
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board desires to call a public hearing on the a doption of a 
final order concerning the extension. 
 
 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby 
authorized to publish and post the attached public notice for a public hearing to be held 
on the 4 th day of February, 2025 at 2:00 p.m.  at the Riverhead Town Hall, 4 West 2 nd 
Street, Riverhead, New York, to hear all interested persons with regard to the adoption 
of a final order concerning the petition for water main extension as described in the 
preambles hereto to provide water service to the properties to be benefitted by the 
proposed Extension No. 97 – Forge Road and designated as District 600, Section 118, 
Block 5, Lots 1.1, 1.2, 2 through 11& 12.1, Section 119, Block 2, Lots 59 through 62, 
and Section 139 Block 1, Lots 1 through 4 on  the Suffolk County Tax Map, Riverhead, 
New York, to be funded through the 2022 Bipartisan Infrastructure Law – Emerging 
Contaminants, The Town Community Preservation Fund, and the payment of key 
money pursuant to the Riverhead Town Code; and 
 
BE IT FURTHE R RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby authorized 
to publish and post a copy of the attached notice in the January 30, 2025 edition of The 
News Review; and be it further    
 
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED , that all Town Hall Departments may review and 
obtain a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a 
certified copy of same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman

FISCAL IMPACT STATEMENT 
OF PROPOSED RIVERHEAD TOWN BOARD LEGISLATION

Re: Riverhead Water District
Booster Pumping Facility at East Winds Drive
H2M Project No.: RDWD2201
Riverhead Capital Project No. 19
Recommendation of Award Contract P
Dear Board Members:
On Thursday, December 19, 2024, the Riverhead Water District receive d bids for the referenced project. A total of 
five (5) bids were submitted for Contract P as indicated on the a ttached bid tabulation. The low Total Alternate Bid 
was submitted by Bensin Contracting, Inc. of Holtsville, New York.
The Total Alternate Bid submitted was in the amount of $1,008,000.00. The alternate bid includes scope relating to 
the replacement of the District’s control valve and swing check  valve for the elevated storage tank at Plant No. 9. 
This scope is critical for the District to optimize the use of their water storage tanks and is recommended to be 
awarded. 
We have reviewed the information submitted by the low bidder an d have found them to be a qualified and 
responsible contractor. Bensin has successfully completed similar work for various water utilities across Long Island
in the past. It is our opinion that Bensin is qualified, and thei r bid prices are fair and responsible. We recommend 
the Town award the contract to the lowest responsible bidder, Bensin Contracting, Inc. of Holtsville, New York,
for the Total Alternate Bid amount of $1,008,000.00.
Upon award of this contract by the Board, we will notify the contractor to obtain the necessary bonds and insurance 
certificates and coordinate with the District’s counsel for sign ing of the contract. Should you have any questions or 
wish to discuss this recommendation, please contact the undersigned at extension 1357.
Very truly yours,
H2M architects + engineers
John R. Collins, P.E.

Recommendation of Award Contract G
Dear Board Members:
On Thursday, December 19, 2024, the Riverhead Water District receive d bids for the referenced project. A total of 
eight (8) bids were submitted for Contract G as indicated on the  attached bid tabulation. The low Total Base Bid 
was submitted by LoDuca Associates, Inc. of Blue Point, New York.
The Total Base Bid submitted was in the amount of$1,002,048.00. H2M completed a cursory call with Chris Young 
and Christopher Perry of LoDuca, on Tuesday, January 7, 2025. LoD uca discussed their experience, project 
approach, and financial status to confirm they understood the p roject scope, schedule, and responsibilities.  
Additionally, LoDuca confirmed that they and their subcontractors meet all apprenticeship training requirements 
listed in the specifications. 
The Total Alternate Bid amount of $1,098,632.00 includes the sc ope related to the recharge basin, driveway, and 
epoxy flooring. However, the basin and driveway work will now b e handled by the Town Highway Department, as 
confirmed with Michael Zaleski on Tuesday, January 7, 2025. Add itionally, the Riverhead Water District has opted 
to omit the epoxy flooring scope.
We have reviewed the information submitted by the low bidder an d have found them to be a qualified and 
responsible contractor. LoDuca has successfully completed similar projects for water utilities across Long Island in 
the past. It is our opinion that LoDuca is qualified, and their bid prices are fair and responsible. We recommend the 
Town award the contract to the lowest responsible bidder, LoDuca Associates, Inc of Blue Point, New York, for 
the Total Base Bid amount of $1,002,048.00.
Upon award of this contract by the Board, we will notify the contractor to obtain the necessary bonds and insurance 
certificates and coordinate with the District’s counsel for sign ing of the contract. Should you have any questions or 
wish to discuss this recommendation, please contact the undersigned at extension 1357.
Very truly yours,
H2M architects + engineers
John R. Collins, P.E.

Recommendation of Award Contract E
Dear Board Members:
On Thursday, December 19, 2024, the Riverhead Water District receive d bids for the referenced project. A total of 
Seven (7) bids were submitted for Contract E as indicated on the attached bid tabulation. The low Total Alternate 
Bid was submitted by MRJ Industries, Inc. of Hampton Bays, New York.
The Total Alternate Bid submitted was in the amount of $1,100,116.00. The alternate bid includes electrical scope 
relating to the replacement of the District’s control valve and  swing check valve for the elevated storage tank at 
Plant No. 9. This scope is critical for the District to optimize the use of their water storage tanks and is recommended 
to be awarded.
H2M and the District conducted a preliminary call with John Fer guson of MRJ on Tuesday, January 7, 2025. This 
will be MRJ's first project for the Riverhead Water District. I n recent years, MRJ has primarily completed projects 
for various school districts and municipalities, including work  with H2M. MRJ brings over 40 years of experience, 
including work in water treatment plants. During the call, MRJ als o discussed their project approach, and financial 
status to confirm they understood the project scope, schedule, and responsibilities. MRJ expressed confidence that 
they have the personnel, knowledge, vendor support, and equipme nt necessary to successfully complete this 
project without delay and to the District’s satisfaction. MRJ con firmed that they and their subcontractors meet all 
apprenticeship training requirements listed in the specificatio ns and will provide supporting documentation. H2M 
also contacted MRJ's project references who all recommended the c ompany, highlighting their ability to complete 
projects on time, communicate effectively, and demonstrate the necessary experience.
Based on our experience with the low bidder and our evaluation of the project references submitted by the low 
bidder we have found them to be a responsible contractor and cap able of performing the project scope. MRJ has 
successfully completed similar projects for water utilities in t he past and similar work for schools and towns across 
Long Island. It is our opinion that MRJ is qualified, and their bid prices are fair and responsible. We recommend the 
Town award the contract to the lowest responsible bidder, MRJ Industries, Inc of Hampton Bays, New York, for 
the Total Alternate Bid amount of $1,100,116.00.
Upon award of this contract by the Board, we will notify the contractor to obtain the necessary bonds and insurance 
certificates and coordinate with the District’s counsel for sign ing of the contract. Should you have any questions or 
wish to discuss this recommendation, please contact the undersigned at extension 1357.
Very truly yours,
H2M architects + engineers
John R. Collins, P.E.

TB Resolution 2025-122 
 
EXTENDS BID NUNC PRO TUNC FOR ELECTRICAL SYSTEM MAINTENANCE AND 
EMERGENCY SERVICE CONTRACT FOR RIVERHEAD WATER DISTRICT 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, Town Board Resolution #2024-137 awarded a bid for ELECTRICAL 
SYSTEM MAINTENANCE AND EMERGENCY SERVICE CONTRACT FOR 
RIVERHEAD WATER DISTRICT, adopted on February 6, 2024 and authorized per the 
terms of the contract until December 31, 2024; and 
 
 WHEREAS, the below-named vendor has agreed to extend the contract for 1 
year as per the bid specification until December 31, 2025 at the original bid amounts for 
the period of January 1 to December 31, 2025; and 
 WHEREAS, the Town Board has reviewed said request. 
 NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the bid ELECTRICAL SYSTEM 
MAINTENANCE AND EMERGENCY SERVICE CONTRACT FOR RIVERHEAD 
WATER DISTRICT be and is hereby extended nunc pro tunc until December 31, 2025; 
and 
 
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be directed to forward a 
certified copy of this resolution to  
 
WIRE TO WATER, INC. 
136 GAZZA BLVD 
FARMINGDALE, NY 11735 
jason@wiretowater.com 
 
with a copy to the Water District and Purchasing Department; and be it further 
 RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
SECONDER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

SECTION 002113 - INFORMATION FOR BIDDERS H2M 
PROPOSAL 
The Proposal contained herein shall be used in making out bids. Any proposal not in accordance with 
these instructions or containing bids not asked for may be rejected. While separate prices are required 
for various items under this contract, it is understood that the contract will be awarded as a whole. 
As the estimates of quantities of items stated in the Proposal are approximate only, bidders are required 
to submit their proposal upon and in the following express conditions, which shall apply and become part 
of every proposal received. 
Bids will be compared by total amounts, said total amount being the sum of the products of the quantities 
multiplied by the unit price bid for the various items, with due consideration being given to the lump sum 
prices bid for any contingent or optional items. Unbalanced bids will not be accepted. 
Each bidder shall fill out in ink, in both words and figures, in the spaces provided, its unit or lump sum bid, 
as the case may be, for each item in said Proposal for which it is submitting a bid. If there is any 
discrepancy between the prices in words and figures, the prices in words shall govern as unit and lump 
sum prices. If the Total Project Cost reported differs from the sum of all individual items, the sum of all 
individual items shall govern. 
A bid which does not include bids for all items in the Proposal may not be considered valid. 
If the contract is not awarded by the Town Board within fourty-five (45) days after the receipt of bids, the 
obligation of the bidder under this Proposal may terminate at its option and it shall thereupon be entitled 
to a refund of its certified check or release of its bid bond furnished by it as security with its proposal. 
BID BOND OR CERTIFIED CHECK 
Each proposal from a Contractor shall be accompanied by a bid bond or certified check on a solvent bank 
of the STATE OF NEW YORK, in the amount of five percent (5%) of the total bid. Such check shall be 
made payable to TOWN OF RIVERHEAD and the amount thereof shall be the measure of liquidated 
damages which the Town may sustain by failure, neglect or refusal of the bidder to execute and deliver 
the contract, should the contract be awarded to it. The checks of all unsuccessful bidders will be 
returned upon the rejection of bids and the awarding of the contract; also, the check of the successful 
bidder will be returned upon the execution of the contract and the furnishing of the required bond. 
NAME OF BIDDER 
Each bidder must state, in its proposal, its full name and business address, and the full name of every 
person, firm or corporation, interested in same, and the address of every person or firm, or president and 
secretary of every corporation, interested with it. 
QUALIFICATIONS OF BIDDERS 
(1) | The Town Board reserves the right to waive any informalities in, or reject any and all bids. 
The Board reserves the right to reject any and all bids which do not conform to the Proposal. 
(2) All bidders must prove to the satisfaction of the Town Board that they are reputable, reliable 
and responsible, and that they possess the necessary qualifications (financial, labor, 
equipment and otherwise) to complete successfully the proposed work.

(3) In determining the qualifications of a bidder, the Town Board will consider its record in the 
performance of any contracts entered into by it for the work contemplated or of similar 
nature, may make such investigation as it deems necessary to determine the ability of the 
bidder to perform the work, and the bidder shall furnish to the Board all such information and

(4) |The Town Board shall be the sole judge of the qualifications of the bidders and of the merits

carry out the obligations of the contract and to complete the work contemplated therein. 
PERFORMANCE AND MAINTENANCE BOND 
The Contractor shall furnish a Performance Bond, Labor and Materials Bond, and a one (1) year 
Maintenance Bond each in an amount equal to one hundred (100%) percent of the total contract price as 
security for its faithful performance of this contract, for the payment of all persons performing labor or 
furnishing materials in connection with this contract. Such bonds shall also cover any penalties, interest 
charges and assessments levied by any governmental unit for failure to comply with laws and/or 
regulations governing public work. The Maintenance Bond shall be an assurance that all work and 
materials provided under this contract shall be maintained for a minimum period of one (1) year. The 
Maintenance Bond shall be furnished following final completion, and payment under the contract.The 
contractor shall be required to furnish all guarantees and warranties of manufacturers of products in 
connection with this contract, but no manufacturer's limitation of time shall act to limit the responsibility of 
the contractor or its surety hereunder. 
The surety must be licensed in the State of New York and have a BEST A rating, or the surety shall 
present information satisfactory to the TOWN/DISTRICT to permit the TOWN/DISTRICT to accept the 
bond. 
At the time of submission of bonds or at any time thereafter, the TOWN/DISTRICT may evaluate the 
surety or sureties proposed, and demand a change of surety if it determines that the financial position of 
such surety does not provide for a proper protection of the interests of the TOWN/DISTRICT. The 
TOWNIDISTRICT shall be guided by its legal counsel, and insurance industry consultants in determining 
proper sureties for TOWN/DISTRICT public works contracts. If the TOWN/DISTRICT notifies the 
contractor in writing that a surety is unacceptable for any reason, then the contractor shall replace the 
surety and the bond in question within five (5) business days with a surety and bond deemed suitable by 
the said TOWN/DISTRICT. The premiums charged for all such bonds shall be a cost of the contractor 
and not the TOWN/DISTRICT. Upon notice to change surety being forwarded to a contractor, no further 
payments shall be made until a new bond in proper form naming an acceptable surety is provided. 
SIGNATURE OF CONTRACTOR 
The bidder to whom a contract may be awarded shall attend at the office of the Town Board, with the 
sureties offered by it, within seven (7) days, (weekends & holidays excepted), after date of notification of 
the acceptance of its proposal, and there sign the contract in quadripartite for the work and furnish 
insurances and approved security for its performance. 
In case of failure to do so, the bidder shall be considered as having abandoned the same, and the check 
accompanying its proposal shall be forfeited to the Town Board, or the penalty of the bid bond shall be 
invoked.

SECTION 004116 - PROPOSAL H2M 
WATER DISTRIBUTION SYSTEM MAINTENANCE RIVERHEAD WATER DISTRICT 
AND EMERGENCY SERVICES CONTRACT TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
H2M PROJECT NO.: RDWD2302 (D) SUFFOLK COUNTY, NEW YORK 
BID DATE: DECEMBER 7, 2023 
WATER DISTRIBUTION SYSTEM MAINTENANCE AND EMERGENCY SERVICES CONTRACT 
SCOPE OF WORK AND PROPOSAL 
1, Location of Work 
Various locations across the service area of the Riverhead Water District, including plant and water 
storage tank sites, public right-of-ways, easements, private communities, etc. within the Town of 
Riverhead, New York. 
Il. Scope of Work 
ds Perform scheduled and emergency distribution system maintenance, repair, and restoration 
services for the Riverhead Water District in accordance with the requirements stipulated herein 
and all prevailing federal, state, and local safety and labor regulations. 
Services may include but not be limited to water main break repair, installation and repair of 
service lines, valve replacement, hydrant replacement, water main replacement, installation of 
water service lines, installation of new water main and pavement repairs. 
Work will be performed on an as-needed basis when authorized by the Water District in 
writing. The District will fax or e-mail a work order outlining the location and nature of work to be 
performed. 
Scheduled maintenance or repair is non-emergency work and will be scheduled by the District at 
least 48 hours in advance of the start of the work. 
Emergency service shall be provided to the Water District on a request basis. For emergency 
service the Contractor shall report to the site in need of service within three (3) hours after 
notification from the Water District including nights, weekends, and holidays. 
Notification from the Water District may also be via phone call (for emergency work) and a 
fax/email transmission of the work order for the service requested. A copy of the work order form 
is included in Appendix A. 
Contractor will be required to maintain the proper bonds and insurance as specified herein. The 
Bonds shall remain in full force and effect for a period of one (1) year after the date of the bond. 
Contractor shall promptly remedy any defects or faults that may occur within twelve (12) months 
after completion and acceptance of the work performed by the Contractor pursuant to this 
Contract. 
The Contractor shall arrange for all mark outs within the public right-of-ways related to the work. 
Where applicable, the District will be responsible for coordination of the required mark-out of 
facilities associated with the MTA/LIRR utility mark-out. 
Contractor shall provide District with dimensional sketch of all work performed for the District's 
tecords prior to payment authorization.
